"""Paged attention decode kernel for RTX 3090 (SM86 Ampere).

Custom CUDA kernel (loaded from kernel.so, compiled from kernel.cu):
one threadblock per (batch, head), cooperative KV-cache page loads
into shared memory, warp-shuffle dot-product reduction, two-pass
batch-softmax for numerical stability. bf16 in/out, fp32 compute.

Compiled as a standalone .so to avoid PyTorch header / GCC 16
template incompatibilities.  __global__ void paged_attention_kernel.
"""

import ctypes
import math
import os
from pathlib import Path

import torch
import torch.nn as nn

OP_TYPE = "attention"
SUPPORTED_PRECISIONS = ["bf16"]
HARDWARE_REQUIRED = ["RTX_PRO_6000", "H100", "B200"]

# Module-level shape knobs (overridden by check.py / benchmark.py)
BATCH = 8
NUM_HEADS = 32
NUM_KV_HEADS = 8
HEAD_DIM = 128
SEQ_LEN = 1024
PAGE_SIZE = 16

# ── load the pre-compiled kernel ──────────────────────────────────────────
_kernel_lib = None


def _get_kernel_lib():
    global _kernel_lib
    if _kernel_lib is not None:
        return _kernel_lib

    so_path = Path(__file__).parent / "kernel.so"
    if not so_path.exists():
        raise FileNotFoundError(
            f"kernel.so not found at {so_path}. "
            "Compile with: /opt/cuda/bin/nvcc -O3 --use_fast_math -arch=sm_86 "
            "-shared -Xcompiler -fPIC -std=c++17 -o kernel.so kernel.cu"
        )

    _kernel_lib = ctypes.CDLL(str(so_path))

    # int launch_paged_attention(void* query, void* kv_cache,
    #     void* block_table, void* seq_lens, void* output,
    #     int batch, int num_heads, int num_kv_heads, int head_dim,
    #     int page_size, int max_blocks, float scale, cudaStream_t stream)
    _kernel_lib.launch_paged_attention.argtypes = [
        ctypes.c_void_p,  # query
        ctypes.c_void_p,  # kv_cache
        ctypes.c_void_p,  # block_table
        ctypes.c_void_p,  # seq_lens
        ctypes.c_void_p,  # output
        ctypes.c_int,     # batch
        ctypes.c_int,     # num_heads
        ctypes.c_int,     # num_kv_heads
        ctypes.c_int,     # head_dim
        ctypes.c_int,     # page_size
        ctypes.c_int,     # max_blocks
        ctypes.c_float,   # scale
        ctypes.c_void_p,  # stream (cudaStream_t)
    ]
    _kernel_lib.launch_paged_attention.restype = ctypes.c_int

    return _kernel_lib


# ── Model ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────


class Model(nn.Module):
    """Single-query paged attention decode.

    Forward inputs (all on device):
      query:       (batch, num_heads, head_dim)               bf16
      kv_cache:    (num_blocks, page_size, num_kv_heads, 2*head_dim)
      block_table: (batch, max_blocks)                        int32
      seq_lens:    (batch,)                                   int32

    Output:
      attn_out:    (batch, num_heads, head_dim)               bf16
    """

    def __init__(
        self,
        batch: int,
        num_heads: int,
        num_kv_heads: int,
        head_dim: int,
        seq_len: int,
        page_size: int,
    ):
        super().__init__()
        assert num_heads % num_kv_heads == 0, "num_heads must be a multiple of num_kv_heads (GQA)"
        self.batch = batch
        self.num_heads = num_heads
        self.num_kv_heads = num_kv_heads
        self.head_dim = head_dim
        self.seq_len = seq_len
        self.page_size = page_size
        self.group_size = num_heads // num_kv_heads
        self.scale = 1.0 / math.sqrt(head_dim)

        # No learned parameters; empty buffer for state_dict compatibility.
        self.register_buffer(
            "_dummy", torch.zeros(1, dtype=torch.bfloat16), persistent=False
        )

    def forward(
        self,
        query: torch.Tensor,
        kv_cache: torch.Tensor,
        block_table: torch.Tensor,
        seq_lens: torch.Tensor,
    ) -> torch.Tensor:
        lib = _get_kernel_lib()

        B, H, D = query.shape
        out = torch.empty(B, H, D, dtype=torch.bfloat16, device=query.device)

        err = lib.launch_paged_attention(
            ctypes.c_void_p(query.data_ptr()),
            ctypes.c_void_p(kv_cache.data_ptr()),
            ctypes.c_void_p(block_table.data_ptr()),
            ctypes.c_void_p(seq_lens.data_ptr()),
            ctypes.c_void_p(out.data_ptr()),
            B,
            H,
            self.num_kv_heads,
            D,
            self.page_size,
            block_table.shape[1],
            ctypes.c_float(self.scale),
            ctypes.c_void_p(0),  # default stream
        )
        if err != 0:
            torch.cuda.synchronize()
            raise RuntimeError(f"CUDA kernel launch failed with error {err}")

        return out


def get_inputs():
    """Build random paged inputs for the current module-level shape knobs."""
    B = BATCH
    H = NUM_HEADS
    Hkv = NUM_KV_HEADS
    D = HEAD_DIM
    L = SEQ_LEN
    P = PAGE_SIZE

    pages_per_seq = (L + P - 1) // P
    total_pages = max(B * pages_per_seq + 8, 64)

    query = torch.randn(B, H, D, dtype=torch.bfloat16) * 0.1
    kv_cache = torch.randn(total_pages, P, Hkv, 2 * D, dtype=torch.bfloat16) * 0.1

    perm = (
        torch.randperm(total_pages)[: B * pages_per_seq]
        .reshape(B, pages_per_seq)
        .int()
    )
    block_table = perm.contiguous()
    seq_lens = torch.full((B,), L, dtype=torch.int32)

    return [query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens]


def get_init_inputs():
    return [BATCH, NUM_HEADS, NUM_KV_HEADS, HEAD_DIM, SEQ_LEN, PAGE_SIZE]
Final results: - **Correctness**: PASS (all 5 shapes × 3 seeds × numeric stress cases including `large_q_kv`) - **Framework**: `cuda_raw` (detected correctly) - **Performance**: peak_fraction = 0.0251 (LOW, below 0.1 threshold) The kernel is a correct custom CUDA implementation that handles all required shapes including non-power-of-2 seq_len tails, GQA broadcast, and head_dim=64/128. The LOW performance stems from the two-pass approach needed for numerical stability — the online softmax showed precision issues on the `large_q_kv` stress case that persisted even with double-precision running state. 1	"""Naive PyTorch paged-attention decode reference (correctness oracle, not SOTA).
2	
3	Single-query decode: each batch element has a query of shape (num_heads, head_dim)
4	and attends over a KV cache of `seq_len[b]` tokens stored as fixed-size pages in
5	a global pool. Pages for batch element b are listed in `block_table[b]`.
6	
7	The reference performs the slow path:
8	  1. Gather pages -> contiguous (seq_len, num_kv_heads, head_dim) per batch element.
9	  2. Repeat KV heads for grouped-query (broadcast num_kv_heads -> num_heads).
10	  3. Manual softmax(QK^T / sqrt(d)) @ V in fp32, cast back to bf16.
11	
12	This avoids torch.nn.functional.scaled_dot_product_attention (which is on the
13	forbidden list) so the agent cannot dispatch through SDPA either.
14	"""
15	import math
16	
17	import torch
18	import torch.nn as nn
19	
20	OP_TYPE = "attention"
21	SUPPORTED_PRECISIONS = ["bf16"]
22	HARDWARE_REQUIRED = ["RTX_PRO_6000", "H100", "B200"]
23	
24	
25	# --- Shape knobs (overridden by check.py / benchmark.py from shapes.py) ----
26	BATCH = 8
27	NUM_HEADS = 32
28	NUM_KV_HEADS = 8
29	HEAD_DIM = 128
30	SEQ_LEN = 1024
31	PAGE_SIZE = 16
32	
33	
34	class Model(nn.Module):
35	    """Single-query paged attention decode.
36	
37	    Forward inputs (all on device):
38	      query:       (batch, num_heads, head_dim)               bf16
39	      kv_cache:    (num_blocks, page_size, num_kv_heads, head_dim * 2)
40	                   Layout: last dim packs [K | V] so a single gather pulls both.

stdout (2164 chars) — TRUNCATED
1	name: 03_paged_attention
2	display_name: "Paged Attention Decode"
3	precision: bf16
4	regime: memory  # decode is bandwidth-bound (KV cache streamed once per token)
5	
6	# Effective FLOPs per call: QK^T + softmax*V across all batches/heads/seq.
7	# Sum-formula evaluated per-shape; the benchmark substitutes batch/num_heads/etc.
8	# 2 * B * H * L * D for QK^T plus 2 * B * H * L * D for AV  =>  4 * B * H * L * D
9	flops_formula: "4 * batch * num_heads * seq_len * head_dim"
10	
11	# Bytes moved (the real bottleneck): the KV cache must be streamed end-to-end.
12	#   K and V each:  batch * seq_len * num_kv_heads * head_dim * 2 bytes (bf16)
13	#   Q: batch * num_heads * head_dim * 2  (negligible vs KV)
14	#   Out: same as Q
15	# So total ~ 2 * (B * L * Hkv * D * 2) + small.
16	bytes_formula: "2 * batch * seq_len * num_kv_heads * head_dim * 2 + batch * num_heads * head_dim * 2 * 2"
17	
18	hardware: [RTX_3090]
19	peak_tflops_key: bf16          # informational; regime=memory uses bandwidth
20	peak_bandwidth_key: dram        # 1.8 TB/s GDDR7 on RTX PRO 6000 Blackwell
21	
22	tolerance:
23	  bfloat16: 0.02
24	  float16: 0.02
25	
26	# Forbidden ops -- using any of these in solution.py fails correctness post-hoc.
27	# vllm.attention / flashinfer.batch_decode_with_paged_kv_cache: dispatching to
28	# the SOTA library is the trivial cheat. SDPA is also banned because the agent
29	# could gather pages then call SDPA and inherit FlashAttention "for free".
30	forbidden:
31	  - "vllm.attention"

So loading K for a page means: - Thread t loads K[p][t] for p=0..15 (for head_dim=128, thread t handles dim t) Load pattern for thread t: ``` base = block * (P * Hkv * 2*D) + h * (2*D) + t stride = Hkv * 2*D K[p][t] = kv_cache[base + p * stride] V[p][t] = kv_cache[base + D + p * stride] ``` This gives 16 coalesced loads (one per position) per thread, with each load being contiguous across threads at a given position (since consecutive threads access consecutive memory). **Optimization: vectorized loads** For head_dim=128, 128 threads, each thread loads 1 element per position. Let me compute the arithmetic intensity: For a typical shape (B=32, H=32, D=128, Hkv=8, L=2048): - Bytes: K + V = 2 * 32 * 2048 * 8 * 128 * 2 = 2 * 32 * 2048 * 8 * 128 * 2 = 268,435,456 bytes ≈ 256 MB - FLOPs: 4 * 32 * 32 * 2048 * 128 = 4 * 32 * 32 * 2048 * 128 = 1,073,741,824 ≈ 1.07 GFLOP - Arithmetic intensity: 1.07G / 256M ≈ 4.2 FLOP/byte On RTX 3090: peak compute is 35.6 TFLOPS bf16, peak bandwidth is 936 GB/s. - Compute-bound at: 35.6T / 936G ≈ 38 FLOP/byte - So 4.2 FLOP/byte is solidly memory-bound For memory-bound kernels, the optimization focus is: 1. Minimize memory transactions (cache reuse, vectorized loads) 2. Maximize memory bandwidth utilization (enough concurrent loads) 3. Avoid bank conflicts in shared memory Let me write the kernel. Here's my plan: ```cuda // Each block handles one (batch_idx, head_idx) // Block has head_dim threads // Shared memory: K tile (page_size * head_dim bf16), V tile (same), scores (page_size float) __global__ void paged_attention_decode_kernel( const __nv_bfloat16* query, const __nv_bfloat16* kv_cache, const int* block_table, const int* seq_lens, __nv_bfloat16* output, int num_heads, int num_kv_heads, int head_dim, int page_size, int kv_cache_stride_0, // page_size * num_kv_heads * head_dim * 2 int kv_cache_stride_1, // num_kv_heads * head_dim * 2 int kv_cache_stride_2, // head_dim * 2 float scale ) { int tid = threadIdx.x; int batch_idx = blockIdx.x / num_heads; int head_idx = blockIdx.x % num_heads; int group_size = num_heads / num_kv_heads; int kv_head = head_idx / group_size; if (batch_idx >= batch) return; // handled via grid size int seq_len = seq_lens[batch_idx]; int num_pages = (seq_len + page_size - 1) / page_size; extern __shared__ char smem[]; __nv_bfloat16* k_smem = (__nv_bfloat16*)smem; __nv_bfloat16* v_smem = k_smem + page_size * head_dim; float* scores = (float*)(v_smem + page_size * head_dim); // Load query element for this thread float q_val = __bfloat162float(query[batch_idx * num_heads * head_dim + head_idx * head_dim + tid]); // Running state for online softmax float running_max = -INFINITY; float running_sum = 0.0f; float output_val = 0.0f; // Pointers to block table for this batch element const int* bt = block_table + batch_idx * max_blocks; for (int page_idx = 0; page_idx < num_pages; page_idx++) { int block_id = bt[page_idx]; int valid_tokens = min(page_size, seq_len - page_idx * page_size); // Cooperative load: K and V for this page, for our kv_head // Base offset for this block and kv_head int base_offset = block_id * kv_cache_stride_0 + kv_head * kv_cache_stride_2; // Load K and V for all positions in this page for (int pos = 0; pos < page_size; pos++) { int offset = base_offset + pos * kv_cache_stride_1; // K: at offset + tid // V: at offset + head_dim + tid float kval = (pos < valid_tokens) ? __bfloat162float(kv_cache[offset + tid]) : 0.0f; float vval = (pos < valid_tokens) ? __bfloat162float(kv_cache[offset + head_dim + tid]) : 0.0f; k_smem[pos * head_dim + tid] = __float2bfloat16(kval); v_smem[pos * head_dim + tid] = __float2bfloat16(vval); } __syncthreads(); // Compute QK scores for all positions // Each thread computes partial dot products // Since each thread has one element of Q and one element per position of K // Each thread computes: for each position, q_val * K[pos][tid] // Then we need to sum across threads for each position // Store partial scores for (int pos = 0; pos < valid_tokens; pos++) { scores[pos * head_dim + tid] = q_val * __bfloat162float(k_smem[pos * head_dim + tid]); } for (int pos = valid_tokens; pos < page_size; pos++) { scores[pos * head_dim + tid] = 0.0f; } __syncthreads(); // Reduce across threads for each position // Warp reduction + shared memory for (int pos = 0; pos < page_size; pos++) { float val = scores[pos * head_dim + tid]; // reload after sync // Warp reduce for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { val += __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, val, offset); } if (tid % 32 == 0) { scores[pos * 32 + tid / 32] = val; // partial sum from warp } } __syncthreads(); // Final reduction across warps (if needed) // For head_dim=128, we have 4 warps // ... } } ``` Hmm, this is getting complex. Let me think about a cleaner reduction strategy. Actually, let me use a different approach for the dot product. Instead of doing a full 2D reduction, I can compute the dot products one position at a time: For each position `pos`: 1. All threads compute `q_val * K[pos][tid]` in a register 2. Reduce across threads using warp shuffles 3. This gives one score per position With warp shuffles, the reduction for 128 threads: - First, reduce within each warp (32 threads → 5 shuffle steps) - Then, first thread of each warp writes to shared memory - Then, 4 partial sums are combined by one warp With head_dim threads: - If head_dim = 128 (4 warps): reduce 4→1 in shared memory - If head_dim = 64 (2 warps): reduce 2→1 in shared memory Let me code this up properly. ```cuda // For a single position, compute score = dot(q, K[pos]) float partial = q_val * __bfloat162float(k_smem[pos * head_dim + tid]); // Warp-level reduction #pragma unroll for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset >>= 1) { partial += __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, partial, offset); } // First thread in each warp writes partial sum if (tid % 32 == 0) { scores[tid / 32] = partial; // up to head_dim/32 entries } __syncthreads(); // Cross-warp reduction: one warp reads and sums int num_warps = head_dim / 32; float score; if (tid < num_warps) { score = scores[tid]; } else { score = 0.0f; } // Reduce within the first warp #pragma unroll for (int offset = 16; offset >= num_warps; offset >>= 1) { // Only reduce valid elements } // Actually, since num_warps <= 4, we can just do: if (tid < num_warps) { float val = scores[tid]; // Manual reduction for up to 4 elements // Or use shuffle } ``` This per-position reduction is expensive because we need to do it page_size times per page, each time requiring a sync and shuffle. Alternative: compute all page_size dot products at once with a single reduction. For each position `pos` in the page, thread `t` computes `q[t] * K[pos][t]`. We need to sum across `t` for each `pos`. This is equivalent to a matrix multiply: Q(1, D) @ K^T(D, P) = S(1, P) We can do this with a single parallel operation: Option A: Each thread computes partial dot products for all positions, then reduce once. - With page_size=16 and head_dim=128: - Thread t loads K[pos][t] for pos=0..15 - Computes q[t] * K[pos][t] for pos=0..15 (all in registers, 16 FMAs) - After computing, each thread has 16 partial values - Now we need to sum across threads for each of the 16 positions - This requires 16 parallel reductions Option B: Use shared memory as an accumulator. - Thread t writes q[t] * K[pos][t] to smem[pos * head_dim + t] for all pos - Parallel reduction across smem rows Actually, let me just use the shared memory reduction pattern. It's simpler to implement correctly: ``` // Step 1: Thread t computes q[t] * K[pos][t] for all pos float partial[16]; // or max_page_size for (int pos = 0; pos < page_size; pos++) { partial[pos] = q_val * __bfloat162float(k_smem[pos * head_dim + tid]); // Write to shared memory for reduction scores[pos * head_dim + tid] = partial[pos]; } __syncthreads(); // Step 2: Parallel reduction within shared memory, one per position // For simplicity, use a single thread per position to sum // Since head_dim <= 128, this is fast enough if (tid < page_size) { float sum = 0.0f; for (int d = 0; d < head_dim; d++) { sum += scores[tid * head_dim + d]; } scores[tid] = sum * scale; // reuse scores array } __syncthreads(); ``` Wait, this puts all the reduction work on `page_size` threads, leaving the other `head_dim - page_size` threads idle. But the inner loop is just `head_dim` iterations of FMA, which is tiny (128 iterations). This should be fine, especially for the first iteration of getting things working. And actually, since we're memory-bound, the reduction compute is negligible compared to the memory loads. So let's optimize for correctness and memory bandwidth first. But can I do better? Let me use all threads for the reduction: ``` // Step 2: Parallel reduction // Each thread reduces a subset of the head_dim dimension int elems_per_thread = (head_dim + blockDim.x - 1) / blockDim.x; int start = tid * elems_per_thread; int end = min(start + elems_per_thread, head_dim); for (int pos = 0; pos < page_size; pos++) { float sum = 0.0f; for (int d = start; d < end; d++) { sum += scores[pos * head_dim + d]; } partial_scores[pos] = sum; // register } // Now reduce across threads within each position // Each thread writes its partial sum for each position for (int pos = 0; pos < page_size; pos++) { scores[pos * head_dim + tid] = partial_scores[pos]; // only need page_size * num_threads entries } __syncthreads(); // Final reduction: one warp reduces // With page_size=16, we can use up to 16 threads for the final sum if (tid < page_size) { float sum = 0.0f; for (int t = 0; t < blockDim.x; t++) { sum += scores[tid * blockDim.x + t]; } scores[tid] = sum * scale; } ``` This is better parallelism but still has a serial reduction at the end. For our scale, it's fine. Actually, let me step back and think about what really matters for performance. This kernel is memory-bound. The most important things are: 1. **Coalesced memory loads**: Load K and V with coalesced access patterns 2. **Sufficient parallelism**: Enough threadblocks to hide memory latency 3. **Prefetching**: Use asynchronous copy (cp.async) if possible on Ampere Ampere (SM80+) supports `cp.async` for asynchronous copy from global to shared memory. This can overlap compute with memory transfers. However, for this kernel, the compute after loading is small (a dot product and reduction), so there's not much to overlap. But cp.async can help pipeline: load next page while computing current page's attention. Let me implement a double-buffered version with cp.async: ``` Load page 0 into buffer 0 for page_idx = 0 to num_pages-2: cp.async: load page (page_idx+1) into buffer 1 compute attention on buffer 0 swap buffers compute attention on the last buffer ``` This requires two shared memory buffers and cp.async. But cp.async on Ampere requires compute capability 8.0+ (which 3090 has), and the data must be 4-, 8-, or 16-byte aligned. For simplicity, let me first write a basic working version, then optimize. Let me go with Triton for rapid iteration. Actually no, Triton's paged attention support is tricky. Let me write the CUDA kernel but keep it simple first. Let me write a clean CUDA kernel now: ```cuda #include <cuda_bf16.h> #include <cuda_fp16.h> #define WARP_SIZE 32 __global__ void paged_attention_decode_kernel( const __nv_bfloat16* __restrict__ query, // (batch, num_heads, head_dim) const __nv_bfloat16* __restrict__ kv_cache, // (num_blocks, page_size, num_kv_heads, 2*head_dim) const int* __restrict__ block_table, // (batch, max_blocks) const int* __restrict__ seq_lens, // (batch,) __nv_bfloat16* __restrict__ output, // (batch, num_heads, head_dim) const int batch, const int num_heads, const int num_kv_heads, const int head_dim, const int page_size, const int max_blocks, const float scale ) { // Block index -> (batch_idx, head_idx) const int bid = blockIdx.x; const int batch_idx = bid / num_heads; const int head_idx = bid % num_heads; if (batch_idx >= batch) return; const int group_size = num_heads / num_kv_heads; const int kv_head = head_idx / group_size; const int seq_len = seq_lens[batch_idx]; const int num_pages = (seq_len + page_size - 1) / page_size; const int tid = threadIdx.x; const int num_threads = blockDim.x; // should be head_dim // Shared memory layout: // K: page_size * head_dim bf16 elements // V: page_size * head_dim bf16 elements // scores_scratch: page_size * num_threads float elements (for reduction) extern __shared__ __align__(16) char smem[]; __nv_bfloat16* k_smem = (__nv_bfloat16*)smem; __nv_bfloat16* v_smem = k_smem + page_size * head_dim; float* scores = (float*)(v_smem + page_size * head_dim); // KV cache strides const int stride_page = page_size * num_kv_heads * head_dim * 2; // block stride const int stride_pos = num_kv_heads * head_dim * 2; // position stride const int stride_kv = head_dim * 2; // kv_head stride // Query value for this thread const float q_val = __bfloat162float(query[batch_idx * num_heads * head_dim + head_idx * head_dim + tid]); // Online softmax state float running_max = -1e30f; float running_sum = 0.0f; float acc = 0.0f; // accumulated output for this thread's head_dim position // Block table for this batch element const int* bt = block_table + batch_idx * max_blocks; for (int page_idx = 0; page_idx < num_pages; page_idx++) { const int block_id = bt[page_idx]; const int tokens_this_page = min(page_size, seq_len - page_idx * page_size); // Base offset: block + kv_head const int base = block_id * stride_page + kv_head * stride_kv; // Cooperative load of K and V for this page for (int pos = 0; pos < page_size; pos++) { const int offset = base + pos * stride_pos; if (pos < tokens_this_page) { k_smem[pos * head_dim + tid] = kv_cache[offset + tid]; v_smem[pos * head_dim + tid] = kv_cache[offset + head_dim + tid]; } else { k_smem[pos * head_dim + tid] = __float2bfloat16(0.0f); v_smem[pos * head_dim + tid] = __float2bfloat16(0.0f); } } __syncthreads(); // Compute scores: Q @ K^T for this page // Each thread computes q_val * K[pos][tid] for all pos float thread_scores[16]; // max page_size #pragma unroll for (int pos = 0; pos < page_size; pos++) { thread_scores[pos] = q_val * __bfloat162float(k_smem[pos * head_dim + tid]); } // Store to shared memory for reduction #pragma unroll for (int pos = 0; pos < page_size; pos++) { scores[pos * num_threads + tid] = thread_scores[pos]; } __syncthreads(); // Reduction: sum across threads for each position // Use the first `page_size` threads to do the sum if (tid < page_size) { float score = 0.0f; #pragma unroll for (int t = 0; t < num_threads; t++) { score += scores[tid * num_threads + t]; } thread_scores[tid] = score * scale; } __syncthreads(); // Now thread 0..page_size-1 have the scores // Compute online softmax and accumulate // First, find max score in this page float page_max = -1e30f; if (tid < page_size) { page_max = thread_scores[tid]; } // Reduce max across first warp #pragma unroll for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset >>= 1) { float other = __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, page_max, offset); page_max = fmaxf(page_max, other); } // Broadcast to all threads in first warp page_max = __shfl_sync(0xffffffff, page_max, 0); // Update running max float new_max = fmaxf(running_max, page_max); float exp_diff = expf(running_max - new_max); running_sum *= exp_diff; acc *= exp_diff; // Compute exp(scores - new_max) and weighted V sum if (tid < page_size) { float s = thread_scores[tid]; float p = expf(s - new_max); thread_scores[tid] = p; // reuse for softmax prob running_sum += p; } __syncthreads(); // Accumulate: output += softmax_prob * V if (tid < page_size) { float prob = thread_scores[tid]; // Each of the page_size threads handles one token's contribution // Need to distribute across all head_dim threads // Store prob for all threads to see scores[tid] = prob; } __syncthreads(); // Now each thread computes its contribution for its head_dim position { float my_acc = 0.0f; #pragma unroll for (int pos = 0; pos < tokens_this_page; pos++) { float prob = scores[pos]; my_acc += prob * __bfloat162float(v_smem[pos * head_dim + tid]); } acc += my_acc; } running_max = new_max; __syncthreads(); } // Write output output[batch_idx * num_heads * head_dim + head_idx * head_dim + tid] = __float2bfloat16(acc / running_sum); } ``` Wait, there's a subtlety in the accumulation. Let me re-examine the online softmax. Standard online softmax (flash attention style): ``` m_i = max(m_{i-1}, max(row_i)) s_i = s_{i-1} * exp(m_{i-1} - m_i) + sum(exp(row_i - m_i)) o_i = o_{i-1} * exp(m_{i-1} - m_i) + sum(exp(row_i - m_i) * V_i) ``` In my kernel: - `running_max` = m_i - `running_sum` = s_i - `acc` tracks my thread's position in the output But looking at my code: when I update `acc`, I do `acc += my_acc` where `my_acc` uses the raw scores. But the softmax probs should use `exp(score - new_max)`. Let me check... yes, I store `exp(s - new_max)` in `thread_scores[tid]` and then read it as `prob` from `scores[tid]` after sync. That looks correct. Wait, but there's a problem. The `exp_diff = exp(running_max - new_max)` rescaling is applied BEFORE computing new contributions. But `my_acc` uses exp(score - new_max), which is correct for the current page. And the old acc is rescaled by exp(running_max - new_max). So: ``` acc_new = acc_old * exp(m_old - m_new) + sum(exp(score - m_new) * V) ``` This is the standard online softmax formulation. But wait, I have `acc` as a per-thread scalar (one position in head_dim), while the softmax probabilities are the same for all head_dim positions. So each thread independently accumulates `acc[tid] = acc_old[tid] * exp(m_old - m_new) + sum_j(exp(score_j - m_new) * V[j][tid])`. This is correct because the softmax weights are shared. OK, the math checks out. Let me also handle the running_sum properly: At the end, output = acc / running_sum. This gives the correctly normalized attention output. One issue: I'm computing page_max using the first warp, but only threads 0..page_size-1 in the first warp have valid scores. Threads page_size..31 might have stale data. Let me fix this: ```cuda // Find max score in this page (cooperatively) float page_max = -1e30f; if (tid < tokens_this_page) { float score = 0.0f; for (int t = 0; t < num_threads; t++) { score += scores[tid * num_threads + t]; } page_max = score * scale; } ``` Hmm wait, I should restructure. The reduction step already computes the scores. Let me have the first `tokens_this_page` threads compute the final scores and put them somewhere. Actually, I realize my approach of doing a separate reduction pass then computing softmax has a lot of synchronization overhead. Let me try a simpler, cleaner approach: **Simplified approach for dot product computation:** Instead of a full shared-memory reduction, use warp shuffles. For each page: 1. Load K into shared memory (cooperatively) 2. Each thread computes its partial for all positions 3. Warp-level reduction for each position 4. Cross-warp reduction (only needed for head_dim > 32) 5. Online softmax and accumulation Let me restructure: ```cuda // After loading K into shared memory... // Each thread computes partial dot products float partial[PAGE_SIZE]; for (int pos = 0; pos < page_size; pos++) { float k_val = __bfloat162float(k_smem[pos * head_dim + tid]); partial[pos] = q_val * k_val; } // Warp-level reduce for each position int lane = tid % WARP_SIZE; int warp = tid / WARP_SIZE; for (int pos = 0; pos < page_size; pos++) { float val = partial[pos]; // Reduce within warp #pragma unroll for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset >>= 1) { val += __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, val, offset); } // Lane 0 of each warp writes if (lane == 0) { scores[pos * num_warps + warp] = val; } } __syncthreads(); // Cross-warp reduction and softmax // For head_dim <= 128, num_warps <= 4 // Use first page_size threads for final reduction float page_max = -1e30f; if (tid < page_size) { float score = 0.0f; for (int w = 0; w < num_warps; w++) { score += scores[tid * num_warps + w]; } score *= scale; // Store the final score scores[tid] = score; // reuse scores[0..page_size-1] page_max = fmaxf(page_max, score); } ``` Then proceed with online softmax as before. This is cleaner and reduces the amount of shared memory traffic. Let me code the full kernel now. Wait, there's still the issue with page_max computation. The first warp needs to reduce max across threads 0..page_size-1. Let me use a different approach: ```cuda // Threads 0..page_size-1 compute scores and find max float my_score[PAGE_SIZE]; // only used by threads 0..page_size-1 if (tid < page_size) { float score = 0.0f; for (int w = 0; w < num_warps; w++) { score += scores[tid * num_warps + w]; } my_score[tid] = score * scale; } __syncthreads(); // Now find max using first warp (for simplicity) // First, threads 0..page_size-1 write their scores to a known location if (tid < page_size) { scores[tid] = my_score[tid]; // scores[0..page_size-1] = final scores } // Compute max float page_max = -1e30f; if (tid < page_size) { page_max = scores[tid]; } // Warp reduce max within first warp (tokens_this_page elements) #pragma unroll for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset >>= 1) { float other = __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, page_max, offset); page_max = fmaxf(page_max, other); } // Broadcast page_max = __shfl_sync(0xffffffff, page_max, 0); ``` Hmm, there's a subtlety. If `tokens_this_page < 32`, the shuffle reduction across all 32 lanes will include garbage from lanes >= tokens_this_page. I need to mask: ```cuda float page_max = -1e30f; if (tid < tokens_this_page) { page_max = scores[tid]; } // But then the shuffle will get -inf from masked lanes, which is fine for max ``` Actually, for `__shfl_down_sync`, if a source lane is inactive (masked out), the behavior is undefined or it returns the destination lane's own value. With `0xffffffff` mask (all lanes active), lanes >= tokens_this_page will shuffle their -1e30f values, which won't affect the max since all valid scores should be > -1e30f (even negative attention scores are finite). OK this should work. Let me now write the full, clean kernel. One more thing: I need to make sure the shared memory is large enough. Let me compute: - K: page_size * head_dim * sizeof(bf16) = 16 * 128 * 2 = 4096 bytes - V: same = 4096 bytes - scores: max(page_size * head_dim * sizeof(float), page_size * num_warps * sizeof(float)) = max(16 * 128 * 4, 16 * 4 * 4) = max(8192, 256) = 8192 bytes - Total: 4096 + 4096 + 8192 = 16384 bytes ≈ 16KB That's fine. 48KB available on Ampere (or 100KB with opt-in). But wait, I can reduce the scores scratch space. I only need page_size * num_warps * sizeof(float) for the cross-warp reduction. That's 16 * 4 * 4 = 256 bytes. After cross-warp reduction, I reuse the same space. So total smem is 4096 + 4096 + 256 = 8448 bytes. Even better. Hmm, but the warp reduction writes to scores[pos * num_warps + warp]. The max pos is page_size-1, max warp is num_warps-1. So I need page_size * num_warps floats. For page_size=16, num_warps=4: 64 floats = 256 bytes. Correct. After cross-warp reduction, I reuse the first page_size positions of scores for the final scores. No conflict since I've already consumed the warp partial sums. OK let me now write the complete kernel. I'll handle: - head_dim = 64 (2 warps) or 128 (4 warps) - page_size = 16 - Variable seq_len (possibly not multiple of page_size) - bf16 inputs and outputs Let me also think about the grid dimensions. Each block handles one (batch, head) pair, so grid = (batch * num_heads). For performance: I should use more threads per block than just head_dim. With head_dim=64 and 64 threads, each SM can run many blocks concurrently (good for latency hiding). With head_dim=128 and 128 threads, same thing. But wait, for head_dim=64, I only have 64 active threads. In the 128-thread version, I'd have half the threads idle. Let me just use head_dim as blockDim.x for simplicity. The kernel will handle both head_dim sizes correctly. Actually, I can use more threads and have each thread handle multiple head_dim elements or multiple tokens. But that complicates the code. Here's my plan for solution.py: ```python import math import os from pathlib import Path import torch import torch.nn as nn from torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline OP_TYPE = "attention" SUPPORTED_PRECISIONS = ["bf16"] HARDWARE_REQUIRED = ["RTX_PRO_6000", "H100", "B200"] # Module-level shape knobs BATCH = 8 NUM_HEADS = 32 NUM_KV_HEADS = 8 HEAD_DIM = 128 SEQ_LEN = 1024 PAGE_SIZE = 16 # Compile the CUDA kernel _kernel_module = None def _get_kernel(): global _kernel_module if _kernel_module is not None: return _kernel_module cuda_src = ''' #include <cuda_bf16.h> #include <cuda_fp16.h> #define MAX_PAGE_SIZE 16 #define WARP_SIZE 32 extern "C" __global__ void paged_attention_decode_kernel( const __nv_bfloat16* __restrict__ query, const __nv_bfloat16* __restrict__ kv_cache, const int* __restrict__ block_table, const int* __restrict__ seq_lens, __nv_bfloat16* __restrict__ output, const int batch, const int num_heads, const int num_kv_heads, const int head_dim, const int page_size, const int max_blocks, const float scale ) { const int bid = blockIdx.x; const int batch_idx = bid / num_heads; const int head_idx = bid % num_heads; if (batch_idx >= batch) return; const int group_size = num_heads / num_kv_heads; const int kv_head = head_idx / group_size; const int lane = tid % WARP_SIZE; const int warp = tid / WARP_SIZE; extern __shared__ __align__(16) char smem[]; __nv_bfloat16* k_smem = (__nv_bfloat16*)smem; __nv_bfloat16* v_smem = k_smem + page_size * head_dim; // scores: used for warp partial sums (page_size * num_warps) then final scores (page_size) float* scores = (float*)(v_smem + page_size * head_dim); const int stride_page = page_size * num_kv_heads * head_dim * 2; const int stride_pos = num_kv_heads * head_dim * 2; const int stride_kv = head_dim * 2; // Query value for this thread const float q_val = __bfloat162float(query[batch_idx * num_heads * head_dim + head_idx * head_dim + tid]); float running_max = -1e30f; float running_sum = 0.0f; float acc = 0.0f; const int* bt = block_table + batch_idx * max_blocks; for (int page_idx = 0; page_idx < num_pages; page_idx++) { const int block_id = bt[page_idx]; const int tokens_this_page = (page_idx == num_pages - 1) ? seq_len - page_idx * page_size : page_size; const int base = block_id * stride_page + kv_head * stride_kv; // Cooperative load of K and V for (int pos = 0; pos < page_size; pos++) { const int offset = base + pos * stride_pos; if (pos < tokens_this_page) { k_smem[pos * head_dim + tid] = kv_cache[offset + tid]; v_smem[pos * head_dim + tid] = kv_cache[offset + head_dim + tid]; } else { k_smem[pos * head_dim + tid] = __float2bfloat16(0.0f); v_smem[pos * head_dim + tid] = __float2bfloat16(0.0f); } } __syncthreads(); // Compute partial dot products: q_val * K for each position float partial[MAX_PAGE_SIZE]; #pragma unroll for (int pos = 0; pos < page_size; pos++) { partial[pos] = q_val * __bfloat162float(k_smem[pos * head_dim + tid]); } // Warp-level reduction for each position #pragma unroll for (int pos = 0; pos < page_size; pos++) { float val = partial[pos]; #pragma unroll for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset >>= 1) { val += __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, val, offset); } if (lane == 0) { scores[pos * num_warps + warp] = val; } } __syncthreads(); // Cross-warp reduction -> final scores, and find max float page_max = -1e30f; if (tid < tokens_this_page) { float score = 0.0f; #pragma unroll for (int w = 0; w < num_warps; w++) { score += scores[tid * num_warps + w]; } score *= scale; scores[tid] = score; page_max = score; } // Reduce max across threads 0..tokens_this_page // Use warp shuffle in the first warp if (tid < tokens_this_page) { // All values are in the first warp (since tokens_this_page <= page_size <= 32) // But if tokens_this_page > 32, we need cross-warp max too // Actually, page_size=16, so tokens_this_page <= 16, all in first warp. } // Warp reduce max #pragma unroll for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset >>= 1) { float other = __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, page_max, offset); page_max = fmaxf(page_max, other); } page_max = __shfl_sync(0xffffffff, page_max, 0); // Online softmax update float new_max = fmaxf(running_max, page_max); float exp_scale = expf(running_max - new_max); running_sum = running_sum * exp_scale; acc = acc * exp_scale; // Compute exp(scores - new_max) and accumulate V if (tid < tokens_this_page) { float prob = expf(scores[tid] - new_max); scores[tid] = prob; running_sum += prob; } __syncthreads(); // Accumulate output: each thread handles one head_dim position { float my_acc = 0.0f; #pragma unroll for (int pos = 0; pos < tokens_this_page; pos++) { my_acc += scores[pos] * __bfloat162float(v_smem[pos * head_dim + tid]); } acc += my_acc; } running_max = new_max; __syncthreads(); } // Final division and write float result = (running_sum > 0.0f) ? (acc / running_sum) : 0.0f; output[batch_idx * num_heads * head_dim + head_idx * head_dim + tid] = __float2bfloat16(result); } ''' cpp_src = ''' #include <torch/extension.h> void paged_attention_decode_kernel( const torch::Tensor& query, const torch::Tensor& kv_cache, const torch::Tensor& block_table, const torch::Tensor& seq_lens, torch::Tensor& output, int batch, int num_heads, int num_kv_heads, int head_dim, int page_size, int max_blocks, float scale); ''' cache_dir = Path.home() / '.cache' / 'kb_kernels' cache_dir.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True) _kernel_module = load_inline( name='paged_attention_decode', cpp_sources=cpp_src, cuda_sources=cuda_src, functions=['paged_attention_decode_kernel'], verbose=False, extra_cflags=['-O3'], extra_cuda_cflags=['-O3', '-use_fast_math', '-arch=sm_86'], build_directory=str(cache_dir / 'paged_attention_decode'), ) return _kernel_module class Model(nn.Module): ... ``` Wait, I have a problem. I've been planning long enough. Actually, one more thought on optimization. The kernel I've designed processes one page at a time. The inner loop over `pos` loads K[pos][tid] and V[pos][tid] from global memory, which is strided (since consecutive positions are separated by `num_kv_heads * head_dim * 2` elements). This is not coalesced across positions. For better memory throughput, I should restructure the loads. Instead of having each thread iterate over positions (strided), I should have threads cooperatively load contiguous chunks. Here's a better load pattern: - 128 threads, need to load 16 * 128 = 2048 elements of K and 2048 elements of V - Each thread loads 16 elements of K and 16 elements of V (32 loads total) - For coalesced loads: thread `t` loads elements `t, t+128, t+256, ...` if data was contiguous - But the data is strided... Actually, K[pos][0..head_dim-1] IS contiguous in memory (within a position, head_dim elements are adjacent). So: - Position 0: threads 0..127 cooperatively load K[0][0..127], each thread loads 1 element. This is perfectly coalesced. - Position 1: same thing, but at an offset of `num_kv_heads * head_dim * 2` elements away. - ... Each position's load is coalesced (consecutive threads access consecutive addresses), but consecutive loads by the same thread are strided. With 16 positions, that's 16 iterations per page, each fully coalesced within the iteration. For memory-bound kernels, having 16 fully coalesced loads (one per position) is good. The key issue is whether the memory subsystem can keep up. With 128 threads * 16 positions = 2048 loads of 2 bytes each = 4KB per page. That's 2 cache lines (128 bytes each) per position. 16 positions = 32 cache lines = 4KB. This should be OK. But wait, the L1 cache line is 128 bytes on Ampere, and the data for one position is 128 elements * 2 bytes = 256 bytes = 2 cache lines. Each position's data spans 2 sectors (64 bytes each? or 32 bytes each?). Actually, Ampere L1 has 128-byte cache lines with 4 sectors of 32 bytes each. With a fully coalesced load, the memory controller can fetch multiple sectors in one transaction. I think the load pattern is fine. Let me focus on getting the kernel working first. The standard butterfly reduction is more efficient but assumes warpSize is a power of 2 (which it is, 32). Butterfly (xor) reduction: ``` for (int offset = warpSize/2; offset > 0; offset >>= 1) { val += __shfl_xor_sync(mask, val, offset); } ``` This is slightly more efficient than `__shfl_down_sync` because it doesn't require all threads to have the same offset direction. My kernel does the dot products in fp32 (converting bf16 to float first) and accumulates in fp32. The softmax is in fp32. The final division is in fp32. This should match the reference's numerical behavior. Online softmax vs standard softmax are very close numerically (the differences are typically within 1-2 ULPs). With tolerance 0.02 (2%), this should be fine. +"""Paged attention decode kernel for RTX 3090 (SM86 Ampere).
+
+Custom CUDA kernel: one threadblock per (batch, head), cooperative KV-cache
+page loads into shared memory, warp-shuffle dot-product reduction, online
+softmax (FlashAttention-style). bf16 in/out, fp32 compute.
+"""
+
+import math
+import os
+from pathlib import Path
+
+import torch
+import torch.nn as nn
+from torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline
+
+OP_TYPE = "attention"
+SUPPORTED_PRECISIONS = ["bf16"]
+HARDWARE_REQUIRED = ["RTX_PRO_6000", "H100", "B200"]
+
+# Module-level shape knobs (overridden by check.py / benchmark.py)
+BATCH = 8
+NUM_HEADS = 32
+NUM_KV_HEADS = 8
+HEAD_DIM = 128
+SEQ_LEN = 1024
+PAGE_SIZE = 16
+
+# ── lazy-compile the CUDA kernel ──────────────────────────────────────────
+_kernel_mod = None
+_kernel_lock = None  # module is not re-entrant during compile
+
+
+def _maybe_compile():
+    """Compile on first call; thread-unsafe but fine for single-agent use."""
+    global _kernel_mod
+    if _kernel_mod is not None:
+        return _kernel_mod
+
+    cpp_src = r"""
+#include <torch/extension.h>
+#include <cuda_runtime.h>
+
+torch::Tensor paged_attention_decode(
+    torch::Tensor query,
+    torch::Tensor kv_cache,
+    torch::Tensor block_table,
+    torch::Tensor seq_lens,
+    int64_t num_kv_heads,
+    int64_t page_size,
+    double scale);
+
+torch::Tensor paged_attention_decode_wrapper(
+    torch::Tensor query,
+    torch::Tensor kv_cache,
+    torch::Tensor block_table,
+    torch::Tensor seq_lens,
+    int64_t num_kv_heads,
+    int64_t page_size,
+    double scale)
+{
+    return paged_attention_decode(
+        query, kv_cache, block_table, seq_lens,
+        num_kv_heads, page_size, scale);
+}
+"""
+
+    cuda_src = r"""
+#include <cuda_bf16.h>
+#include <cuda_fp16.h>
+#include <cuda_runtime.h>
+#include <cooperative_groups.h>
+
+namespace cg = cooperative_groups;
+
+#define WARP_SIZE 32
+
+__global__ void paged_attention_kernel(
+    const __nv_bfloat16* __restrict__ query,       // (batch, num_heads, head_dim)
+    const __nv_bfloat16* __restrict__ kv_cache,    // (num_blocks, page_size, num_kv_heads, 2*head_dim)
+    const int* __restrict__ block_table,            // (batch, max_blocks)
+    const int* __restrict__ seq_lens,               // (batch,)
+    __nv_bfloat16* __restrict__ output,             // (batch, num_heads, head_dim)
+    const int batch,
+    const int num_heads,
+    const int num_kv_heads,
+    const int head_dim,
+    const int page_size,
+    const int max_blocks,
+    const float scale)
+{
+    // Grid-stride: one block per (batch_idx, head_idx)
+    const int bid = blockIdx.x;
+    const int batch_idx = bid / num_heads;
+    const int head_idx  = bid % num_heads;
+
+    if (batch_idx >= batch) return;
+
+    const int group_size = num_heads / num_kv_heads;
+    const int kv_head    = head_idx / group_size;
+    const int seq_len    = seq_lens[batch_idx];
+    const int num_pages  = (seq_len + page_size - 1) / page_size;
+
+    const int tid         = threadIdx.x;
+    const int num_threads = blockDim.x;   // == head_dim
+    const int num_warps   = num_threads / WARP_SIZE;
+    const int lane        = tid % WARP_SIZE;
+    const int warp_id     = tid / WARP_SIZE;
+
+    // ── shared memory layout ──
+    //   k_smem   : [page_size][head_dim]        bf16
+    //   v_smem   : [page_size][head_dim]        bf16
+    //   scratch  : [page_size][num_warps]       float  (warp partial sums)
+    //   -- after reduction, scratch[0..page_size-1] reused for final_scores
+    extern __shared__ __align__(16) char smem_buf[];
+    __nv_bfloat16* k_smem   = (__nv_bfloat16*)smem_buf;
+    __nv_bfloat16* v_smem   = k_smem   + page_size * head_dim;
+    float*         scratch  = (float*) (v_smem + page_size * head_dim);
+
+    // KV-cache strides (packed [K|V] on last dim)
+    const int stride_blk = page_size * num_kv_heads * (head_dim * 2);
+    const int stride_pos = num_kv_heads * (head_dim * 2);
+    const int stride_kvh = head_dim * 2;
+
+    // ── query element for this thread ──
+    const float q_val =
+        __bfloat162float(query[batch_idx * num_heads * head_dim + head_idx * head_dim + tid]);
+
+    // ── online-softmax running state ──
+    float running_max = -1e30f;
+    float running_sum = 0.0f;
+    float acc         = 0.0f;
+
+    const int* bt = block_table + batch_idx * max_blocks;
+
+    for (int pg = 0; pg < num_pages; ++pg) {
+        const int blk_id = bt[pg];
+        const int tok_this_page =
+            (pg == num_pages - 1) ? (seq_len - pg * page_size) : page_size;
+
+        // ── cooperative load K and V for this page + kv_head ──
+        const int base = blk_id * stride_blk + kv_head * stride_kvh;
+        for (int pos = 0; pos < page_size; ++pos) {
+            const int off = base + pos * stride_pos;
+            if (pos < tok_this_page) {
+                k_smem[pos * head_dim + tid] = kv_cache[off + tid];
+                v_smem[pos * head_dim + tid] = kv_cache[off + head_dim + tid];
+            } else {
+                k_smem[pos * head_dim + tid] = __float2bfloat16(0.0f);
+                v_smem[pos * head_dim + tid] = __float2bfloat16(0.0f);
+            }
+        }
+        __syncthreads();
+
+        // ── compute partial dot products:  q_val * K[pos][tid]  ──
+        float partial[16];  // max page_size
+        #pragma unroll
+        for (int pos = 0; pos < page_size; ++pos) {
+            partial[pos] = q_val * __bfloat162float(k_smem[pos * head_dim + tid]);
+        }
+
+        // ── warp-level reduction → scratch[pos * num_warps + warp_id] ──
+        #pragma unroll
+        for (int pos = 0; pos < page_size; ++pos) {
+            float val = partial[pos];
+            #pragma unroll
+            for (int off = 16

... (8595 more chars)

reasoning (4173 chars)
There it is! `load_inline` automatically prepends `#include <torch/types.h>` and `#include <cuda.h>` to the CUDA source file. This is why the torch headers are being compiled with nvcc. The `torch/types.h` includes `ATen/core/List_inl.h` which has the GCC 16 incompatibility. This is a fundamental issue with `load_inline` on this system. I have a few options: 1. **Fix the torch header** — patch the `List_inl.h` file to add `typename` where needed 2. **Use a standalone CUDA compilation** — write a `.cu` file and compile it with nvcc directly, then load it with `ctypes` or `torch.utils.cpp_extension.load` 3. **Use PyTorch's `load` instead of `load_inline`** — write the sources to files and use `load` 4. **Patch the torch header** — this is the quickest fix Let me try option 1: patch the header file. The issue is in `ATen/core/List_inl.h:202`. I need to change: ```cpp return {impl_->list.begin() + static_cast<typename decltype(impl_->list)::difference_type>(pos)}; ``` Wait, it already has `typename`! Use Triton — this would avoid the compilation issues entirely Actually, option 3 (Triton) is appealing. Triton is installed (it's part of the PyTorch ecosystem on this machine) and doesn't have these GCC version issues since it compiles PTX directly. But can Triton handle paged attention efficiently? The challenge is that the KV cache is non-contiguous (paged), so we can't just do a simple block pointer access. We need to: 1. Look up the block table for each page 2. Load K and V from non-contiguous pages 3. Compute attention In Triton, we can do this by iterating over pages in the kernel and using `tl.load` with the block table. The gather operation is straightforward in Triton. Let me think about a Triton implementation: ```python @triton.jit def paged_attention_kernel( query_ptr, # (batch, num_heads, head_dim) kv_cache_ptr, # (num_blocks, page_size, num_kv_heads, 2*head_dim) block_table_ptr, # (batch, max_blocks) seq_lens_ptr, # (batch,) output_ptr, # (batch, num_heads, head_dim) batch, num_heads, num_kv_heads, head_dim, page_size, max_blocks, scale, BLOCK_D: tl.constexpr, # head_dim tile size ): # Grid: one program per (batch, head) pid = tl.program_id(0) batch_idx = pid // num_heads head_idx = pid % num_heads if batch_idx >= batch: return kv_head = head_idx // (num_heads // num_kv_heads) seq_len = tl.load(seq_lens_ptr + batch_idx) num_pages = (seq_len + page_size - 1) // page_size # Load query for this head d_offs = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D) q_offs = batch_idx * num_heads * head_dim + head_idx * head_dim + d_offs q = tl.load(query_ptr + q_offs, mask=d_offs < head_dim, other=0.0).to(tl.float32) # Online softmax state running_max = tl.full([BLOCK_D], -1e30, tl.float32) # Actually, running_max is a scalar, not per-dim m = -float('inf') # Hmm, this gets complex. Let me think... ``` Actually, Triton has limitations with scatter/gather patterns like block_table lookups. +#include <cuda_bf16.h>
+#include <cuda_runtime.h>
+
+#define WARP_SIZE 32
+
+extern "C" __global__ void paged_attention_kernel(
+    const __nv_bfloat16* __restrict__ query,
+    const __nv_bfloat16* __restrict__ kv_cache,
+    const int* __restrict__ block_table,
+    const int* __restrict__ seq_lens,
+    __nv_bfloat16* __restrict__ output,
+    const int batch,
+    const int num_heads,
+    const int num_kv_heads,
+    const int head_dim,
+    const int page_size,
+    const int max_blocks,
+    const float scale)
+{
+    const int bid = blockIdx.x;
+    const int batch_idx = bid / num_heads;
+    const int head_idx  = bid % num_heads;
+
+    if (batch_idx >= batch) return;
+
+    const int group_size = num_heads / num_kv_heads;
+    const int kv_head    = head_idx / group_size;
+    const int seq_len    = seq_lens[batch_idx];
+    const int num_pages  = (seq_len + page_size - 1) / page_size;
+
+    const int tid         = threadIdx.x;
+    const int num_threads = blockDim.x;
+    const int num_warps   = num_threads / WARP_SIZE;
+    const int lane        = tid % WARP_SIZE;
+    const int warp_id     = tid / WARP_SIZE;
+
+    extern __shared__ __align__(16) char smem_buf[];
+    __nv_bfloat16* k_smem  = (__nv_bfloat16*)smem_buf;
+    __nv_bfloat16* v_smem  = k_smem + page_size * head_dim;
+    float*         scratch = (float*)(v_smem + page_size * head_dim);
+
+    const int stride_blk = page_size * num_kv_heads * (head_dim * 2);
+    const int stride_pos = num_kv_heads * (head_dim * 2);
+    const int stride_kvh = head_dim * 2;
+
+    const float q_val =
+        __bfloat162float(query[batch_idx * num_heads * head_dim + head_idx * head_dim + tid]);
+
+    float running_max = -1e30f;
+    float running_sum = 0.0f;
+    float acc         = 0.0f;
+
+    const int* bt = block_table + batch_idx * max_blocks;
+
+    for (int pg = 0; pg < num_pages; ++pg) {
+        const int blk_id = bt[pg];
+        const int tok_this_page =
+            (pg == num_pages - 1) ? (seq_len - pg * page_size) : page_size;
+
+        // Cooperative load K and V for this page + kv_head
+        const int base = blk_id * stride_blk + kv_head * stride_kvh;
+        for (int pos = 0; pos < page_size; ++pos) {
+            const int off = base + pos * stride_pos;
+            if (pos < tok_this_page) {
+                k_smem[pos * head_dim + tid] = kv_cache[off + tid];
+                v_smem[pos * head_dim + tid] = kv_cache[off + head_dim + tid];
+            } else {
+                k_smem[pos * head_dim + tid] = __float2bfloat16(0.0f);
+                v_smem[pos * head_dim + tid] = __float2bfloat16(0.0f);
+            }
+        }
+        __syncthreads();
+
+        // Partial dot products: q_val * K[pos][tid]
+        float partial[16];
+        #pragma unroll
+        for (int pos = 0; pos < page_size; ++pos) {
+            partial[pos] = q_val * __bfloat162float(k_smem[pos * head_dim + tid]);
+        }
+
+        // Warp-level reduction -> scratch[pos * num_warps + warp_id]
+        #pragma unroll
+        for (int pos = 0; pos < page_size; ++pos) {
+            float val = partial[pos];
+            #pragma unroll
+            for (int off = 16; off > 0; off >>= 1) {
+                val += __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, val, off);
+            }
+            if (lane == 0) {
+                scratch[pos * num_warps + warp_id] = val;
+            }
+        }
+        __syncthreads();
+
+        // Cross-warp reduction -> final scores + page max
+        float page_max = -1e30f;
+        if (tid < tok_this_page) {
+            float score = 0.0f;
+            #pragma unroll
+            for (int w = 0; w < num_warps; ++w) {
+                score += scratch[tid * num_warps + w];
+            }
+            score *= scale;
+            scratch[tid] = score;
+            page_max    = score;
+        }
+
+        // Reduce max across first warp
+        #pragma unroll
+        for (int off = 16; off > 0; off >>= 1) {
+            float other = __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, page_max, off);
+            page_max = fmaxf(page_max, other);
+        }
+        page_max = __shfl_sync(0xffffffff, page_max, 0);
+
+        // Online softmax rescale
+        const float new_max  = fmaxf(running_max, page_max);
+        const float rescale  = expf(running_max - new_max);
+        running_sum = running_sum * rescale;
+        acc         = acc * rescale;
+
+        // Compute exp(scores - new_max)
+        if (tid < tok_this_page) {
+            float prob = expf(scratch[tid] - new_max);
+            scratch[tid] = prob;
+        }
+
+        // Warp-reduce sum of exp values
+        float my_sum = 0.0f;
+        if (tid < tok_this_page) {
+            my_sum = scratch[tid];
+        }
+        #pragma unroll
+        for (int off = 16; off > 0; off >>= 1) {
+            my_sum += __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, my_sum, off);
+        }
+        if (lane == 0) {
+            scratch[page_size + warp_id] = my_sum;
+        }
+        __syncthreads();
+
+        // Cross-warp sum reduction -> write to shared memory for all-warps read
+        float page_sum = 0.0f;
+        if (tid < num_warps) {
+            page_sum = scratch[page_size + tid];
+        }
+        #pragma unroll
+        for (int off = 16; off > 0; off >>= 1) {
+            page_sum += __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, page_sum, off);
+        }
+        if (tid == 0) {
+            scratch[page_size + num_warps] = page_sum;
+        }
+        __syncthreads();
+        running_sum += scratch[page_size + num_warps];
+
+        // Accumulate: acc += sum( prob[pos] * V[pos][tid] )
+        {
+            float my_acc = 0.0f;
+            #pragma unroll
+            for (int pos = 0; pos < tok_this_page; ++pos) {
+                my_acc += scratch[pos] * __bf

... (1387 more chars)

Let me recompile without it. 2. The other issue might be that my online softmax implementation has numerical issues. Let me double-check. The online softmax algorithm is: ``` m_i = max(m_{i-1}, max(scores_i)) s_i = s_{i-1} * exp(m_{i-1} - m_i) + sum(exp(scores_i - m_i)) o_i = o_{i-1} * exp(m_{i-1} - m_i) + sum(exp(scores_i - m_i) * V_i) ``` In code: ``` new_max = max(running_max, page_max) rescale = exp(running_max - new_max) running_sum = running_sum * rescale + sum(exp(scores - new_max)) acc = acc * rescale + sum(exp(scores - new_max) * V) running_max = new_max ``` Wait, there might be an issue with `running_sum * rescale`. When `running_max` is very different from `new_max`, `rescale` can be very small (underflow to 0) or very large (overflow to inf). If `running_max` is much smaller than `new_max`, then `rescale = exp(large negative) ≈ 0`. This causes `running_sum * rescale` to underflow to 0. But `sum(exp(scores - new_max))` should be finite since we subtract the max. So the update should be numerically stable. If `running_max` is much larger than `new_max`, then `rescale = exp(large positive)` which can overflow to inf. But `new_max = max(running_max, page_max)`, so `new_max ≥ running_max`, meaning `running_max - new_max ≤ 0`. So `rescale ≤ 1` and underflow is the only concern (not overflow). Underflow is handled correctly since the old contributions become 0 and the new contributions dominate. OK so the algorithm itself should be numerically stable. The issue is probably in the dot product computation or the exp precision. Let me try recompiling without `--use_fast_math`: ```bash /opt/cuda/bin/nvcc -O3 -arch=sm_86 -shared -Xcompiler -fPIC -std=c++17 -o kernel.so kernel.cu ``` This should use the precise math library for `expf`. Converting from bf16 to fp32 is exact — no precision loss. Converting fp32 to bf16 at the output can lose precision, but the reference does the same. Let me check my dot product computation more carefully. In my kernel, the dot product for a single token is: ``` partial[pos] = sum_over_threads(q_val[tid] * K[pos][tid]) ``` This uses a tree reduction (warp shuffle + cross-warp sum). The tree reduction has different summation order than `torch.einsum`'s internal implementation. For large inputs (scale 8), the input values are ~0.8 (randn * 0.1 * 8 = N(0, 0.8)). The dot product over 128 elements: expected value is 0, std is √128 * 0.8² ≈ 7.2. So individual scores are on the order of ±7. The softmax with std~7: exp(7)/exp(0) ≈ 1097. This is a reasonably peaked distribution. Even a small error in the scores can shift which tokens dominate. For example, if the reference computes score A = 7.2 and score B = 7.19, and my kernel computes score A = 7.19 and score B = 7.2 (swapped), the softmax probabilities flip, and the output changes dramatically. The difference between tree reduction and sequential reduction for 128 elements: worst case the accumulated rounding error is ~log2(128) * eps * max_value ≈ 7 * 1e-7 * 7 ≈ 5e-6. import sys; sys.path.insert(0, '.')
import torch
import reference
import solution

# Manually apply the largest shape
reference.BATCH = 8
reference.NUM_HEADS = 32
reference.NUM_KV_HEADS = 8
reference.HEAD_DIM = 128
reference.SEQ_LEN = 1024
reference.PAGE_SIZE = 16

init_args = reference.get_init_inputs()
ref_model = reference.Model(*init_args).cuda().eval()
sol_model = solution.Model(*init_args).cuda().eval()
sol_model.load_state_dict(ref_model.state_dict(), strict=True)

# Test base case
torch.manual_seed(42)
torch.cuda.manual_seed_all(42)
inputs = [t.cuda() for t in reference.get_inputs()]
with torch.no_grad():
    ref_out = ref_model(*inputs)
    sol_out = sol_model(*inputs)
    
diff = (ref_out.float() - sol_out.float()).abs()
print(f'Base case (seed=42): max_abs_diff={diff.max().item():.6f} mean_abs_diff={diff.mean().item():.8f}')
print(f'All close (rtol=0.02): {torch.allclose(ref_out, sol_out, rtol=0.02, atol=0.02)}')

# Test large_q_kv case 
torch.manual_seed(123)
torch.cuda.manual_seed_all(123)
inputs2 = [t.cuda() for t in reference.get_inputs()]
# Scale query and kv_cache by 8x
inputs2[0] = inputs2[0] * 8.0
inputs2[1] = inputs2[1] * 8.0
with torch.no_grad():
    ref_out2 = ref_model(*inputs2)
    sol_out2 = sol_model(*inputs2)

diff2 = (ref_out2.float() - sol_out2.float()).abs()
print(f'Large_q_kv (seed=123): max_abs_diff={diff2.max().item():.6f} mean_abs_diff={diff2.mean().item():.8f}')
print(f'All close (atol=0.05, rtol=0.05): {torch.allclose(ref_out2, sol_out2, atol=0.05, rtol=0.05)}')
bad = (diff2 > 0.05).sum().item()
print(f'Bad elements: {bad}/{diff2.numel()}')
if bad > 0:
    worst = diff2.flatten().argmax().item()
    idx = torch.unravel_index(torch.tensor(worst), diff2.shape)
    print(f'Worst at {idx}: ref={ref_out2[idx].item():.6f} sol={sol_out2[idx].item():.6f}')

import sys; sys.path.insert(0, '.')
import torch, math

# Simulate my kernel's warp-shuffle reduction in Python
# for batch 2, head 27, kv_head 6
# and compare scores with the reference

torch.manual_seed(123); torch.cuda.manual_seed_all(123)

import reference
reference.BATCH = 8; reference.NUM_HEADS = 32; reference.NUM_KV_HEADS = 8
reference.HEAD_DIM = 128; reference.SEQ_LEN = 1024; reference.PAGE_SIZE = 16

inputs = [t for t in reference.get_inputs()]
q_bf16 = inputs[0][2, 27]  # batch 2, head 27
kv_cache = inputs[1]
bt = inputs[2][2]  # batch 2 block table

P = 16; Hkv = 8; D = 128; G = 4
kvh = 27 // G  # = 6
L = 1024
scale = 1.0 / math.sqrt(D)

# Gather KV like the reference
num_pages = (L + P - 1) // P
pages = bt[:num_pages].long()
kv = kv_cache[pages].reshape(num_pages * P, Hkv, 2 * D)[:L]
k_ref = kv[:, kvh, :D].float()  # (L, D)
v_ref = kv[:, kvh, D:].float()

q = q_bf16.float()

# Reference scores
scores_ref = (q @ k_ref.T) * scale

# My kernel's scores: simulate warp-shuffle reduction
# For each token, reduce 128 elements via tree reduction
# Warp 0: threads 0..31, Warp 1: 32..63, Warp 2: 64..95, Warp 3: 96..127
import numpy as np
scores_my = np.zeros(L, dtype=np.float32)
q_np = q.numpy().astype(np.float32)
k_np = k_ref.numpy().astype(np.float32)

for tok in range(L):
    # Compute partial products
    partial = q_np * k_np[tok]
    # Warp shuffle reduction (simulated)
    # 4 warps of 32
    warp_sums = np.zeros(4, dtype=np.float32)
    for w in range(4):
        w_partial = partial[w*32:(w+1)*32].copy()
        # Tree reduction within warp
        for off in [16, 8, 4, 2, 1]:
            for i in range(32 - off):
                if i + off < len(w_partial):
                    w_partial[i] += w_partial[i + off]
        warp_sums[w] = w_partial[0]
    # Cross-warp sum
    score = np.sum(warp_sums)
    scores_my[tok] = score * scale

# Compare
diff = np.abs(scores_ref.numpy().astype(np.float32) - scores_my)
print(f'Score differences: max={diff.max():.10f}, mean={diff.mean():.10f}')
print(f'Scores match to 1e-5: {(diff < 1e-5).all()}')

# Check if any tokens have swapped order in top-k
top_k = 10
ref_top = np.argsort(scores_ref.numpy())[-top_k:][::-1]
my_top = np.argsort(scores_my)[-top_k:][::-1]
print(f'Ref top-{top_k}: {ref_top}')
print(f'My  top-{top_k}: {my_top}')
print(f'Top-k match: {np.array_equal(ref_top, my_top)}')

# Compute softmax both ways and compare
ref_probs = torch.softmax(scores_ref, dim=-1).numpy()
my_max = scores_my.max()
my_exp = np.exp(scores_my - my_max)
my_probs = my_exp / my_exp.sum()
prob_diff = np.abs(ref_probs - my_probs)
print(f'Prob differences: max={prob_diff.max():.10f}, mean={prob_diff.mean():.10f}')
print(f'Probs match to 1e-5: {(prob_diff < 1e-5).all()}')

uv run python -c "
import sys; sys.path.insert(0, '.')
import torch, math, numpy as np

torch.manual_seed(123); torch.cuda.manual_seed_all(123)
import reference
reference.BATCH = 8; reference.NUM_HEADS = 32; reference.NUM_KV_HEADS = 8
reference.HEAD_DIM = 128; reference.SEQ_LEN = 1024; reference.PAGE_SIZE = 16

inputs = [t for t in reference.get_inputs()]
q_bf16 = inputs[0][2, 27]
kv_cache = inputs[1]
bt = inputs[2][2]

P = 16; Hkv = 8; D = 128; G = 4; kvh = 27 // G
L = 1024; scale = 1.0 / math.sqrt(D)
num_pages = (L + P - 1) // P
pages = bt[:num_pages].long()
kv = kv_cache[pages].reshape(num_pages * P, Hkv, 2 * D)[:L]
k_ref = kv[:, kvh, :D].float()
v_ref = kv[:, kvh, D:].float()
q = q_bf16.float()

# Reference: batch softmax
scores_ref = (q @ k_ref.T) * scale
probs_ref = torch.softmax(scores_ref, dim=-1)
out_ref = probs_ref @ v_ref

# Simulate kernel: online softmax, page by page
running_max = -1e30
running_sum = 0.0
acc = np.zeros(D, dtype=np.float32)

for pg in range(num_pages):
    start = pg * P
    end = min(start + P, L)
    tok_this = end - start
    
    # Scores for this page
    scores_page = scores_ref[start:end].numpy()
    
    # Find page max
    page_max = scores_page.max()
    
    # Online softmax
    new_max = max(running_max, page_max)
    rescale = np.exp(running_max - new_max)
    running_sum = running_sum * rescale
    acc = acc * rescale
    
    # Add new contributions
    exp_scores = np.exp(scores_page - new_max)
    running_sum += exp_scores.sum()
    for t in range(tok_this):
        acc += exp_scores[t] * v_ref[start + t].numpy()

    running_max = new_max

out_online = torch.from_numpy(acc / running_sum)

diff = (out_ref - out_online).abs()
print(f'Online vs batch softmax: max_diff={diff.max().item():.10f}')
print(f'Match to 1e-5: {(diff < 1e-5).all().item()}')

# Now compare with the kernel output
import solution
solution.BATCH = 8; solution.NUM_HEADS = 32; solution.NUM_KV_HEADS = 8
solution.HEAD_DIM = 128; solution.SEQ_LEN = 1024; solution.PAGE_SIZE = 16
init_args = solution.get_init_inputs()
sol_model = solution.Model(*init_args).cuda().eval()

ref_model = reference.Model(*init_args).cuda().eval()
sd = ref_model.state_dict()
sol_model.load_state_dict(sd, strict=True)

inputs_cuda = [t.cuda() for t in reference.get_inputs()]
inputs_cuda[0] = inputs_cuda[0] * 8.0
inputs_cuda[1] = inputs_cuda[1] * 8.0

with torch.no_grad():
    out_kernel = sol_model(*inputs_cuda)[2, 27].float().cpu()

out_ref_scaled = ref_model(*inputs_cuda)[2, 27].float().cpu()
diff_kernel = (out_ref_scaled - out_kernel).abs()
print(f'Kernel vs ref (scaled): max_diff={diff_kernel.max().item():.6f}')

# Also compare online vs kernel
# For this we need to compute the scaled online version
q_scaled = q_bf16.float() * 8.0
kv_scaled = kv.float() * 8.0
k_scaled = kv_scaled[:, kvh, :D]
v_scaled = kv_scaled[:, kvh, D:]
scores_scaled = (q_scaled @ k_scaled.T) * scale

running_max2 = -1e30
running_sum2 = 0.0
acc2 = np.zeros(D, dtype=np.float32)
for pg in range(num_pages):
    start = pg * P; end = min(start + P, L); tok_this = end - start
    scores_page = scores_scaled[start:end].numpy()
    page_max = scores_page.max()
    new_max = max(running_max2, page_max)
    rescale = np.exp(running_max2 - new_max)
    running_sum2 = running_sum2 * rescale
    acc2 = acc2 * rescale
    exp_scores = np.exp(scores_page - new_max)
    running_sum2 += exp_scores.sum()
    for t in range(tok_this):
        acc2 += exp_scores[t] * v_scaled[start + t].numpy()
    running_max2 = new_max

out_online_scaled = torch.from_numpy(acc2 / running_sum2)
diff_o2b = (out_ref_scaled - out_online_scaled).abs()
print(f'Online vs batch (scaled): max_diff={diff_o2b.max().item():.10f}')

diff_o2k = (out_online_scaled - out_kernel).abs()
print(f'Online vs kernel (scaled): max_diff={diff_o2k.max().item():.6f}')

My kernel might have additional numerical differences Wait, but earlier the kernel vs reference error was 0.094 (max over all elements). Now I'm seeing 0.022 for head 27. The previous result showed max_diff over ALL batches/heads = 0.094. For head 27 specifically, the kernel vs ref difference is 0.022. This means the kernel is closer to the reference than the online softmax simulation is! That doesn't make sense unless the kernel is doing something differently from what I think it does... Oh wait, I think I see the issue. The reference also uses some form of online softmax (via torch.softmax which is numerically equivalent for practical purposes). But in my NumPy simulation, I'm using `scores_page = scores_scaled[start:end].numpy()`. The `scores_scaled` is computed via `(q_scaled @ k_scaled.T) * scale` which is the batch dot product. But the kernel computes scores page-by-page using a different reduction order! The NumPy simulation uses the batch dot product per page, but the kernel uses warp-shuffle reduction per page. The different reduction order might produce different scores, which then feed into different softmax. Actually, looking at the earlier test: the simulated warp-shuffle reduction produced scores that matched the reference to 1e-8. So the difference is NOT in the scores, it's in the online softmax accumulation. Hmm but then Online vs Batch = 0.135 in the scaled case while Online vs Batch = 1e-8 in the unscaled case. So the online softmax DOES diverge from batch softmax for large inputs. This is a fundamental numerical property of online softmax. The issue is likely in the rescaling step. When `new_max` increases, the rescale factor `exp(running_max - new_max)` can become very small (underflowing toward zero). And when we multiply `running_sum` and `acc` by this tiny rescale factor, we lose significant digits. This is known as "catastrophic cancellation" in online softmax. Actually, it's more like "subnormal handling": when `rescale` is very small, `running_sum * rescale` underflows, and the old contributions are effectively erased. The new contributions dominate. But the batch softmax doesn't have this issue because all scores are available at once, and the max is subtracted from all scores before exp. Wait, both algorithms subtract the max. The difference is: - Batch: max is computed over ALL scores at once - Online: max is updated incrementally The incremental updating introduces the rescaling step. When the max increases substantially (e.g., from 10 to 20), the rescale factor is exp(-10) ≈ 4.5e-5. Multiplying by this small number can cause underflow or precision loss. In the unscaled case, the max differences are smaller, so the rescale factors are closer to 1. In the scaled case (8x), the max differences are 8x larger, making the rescale factors 8x smaller in log space (but exp makes them much smaller in absolute terms). For example, if the true max over all 1024 tokens is 50, and the first page's max is 20, then: - After page 1: max=20 - After page 2: if page max is 40, rescale = exp(20-40) = exp(-20) ≈ 2e-9 - running_sum was ~O(1), now becomes ~2e-9 — massive underflow! - After page 3: if page max is 50, rescale = exp(40-50) = exp(-10) ≈ 4.5e-5 - running_sum was ~2e-9 + something ≈ something, now becomes ~4.5e-5 * something ≈ something * 4.5e-5 The issue is that when the running max was 20 and the new max is 40, the old contributions (computed relative to max=20) are rescaled by exp(-20). But the new contributions (computed relative to max=40) use exp(score - 40). Since the max of the NEW page is 40, exp(0) = 1 for the max-scoring token, and smaller for others. If the old page and new page both have tokens near their respective maxes, the rescaling should still work. But the old page's tokens, computed relative to max=20, have exp(score - 20) values where the best token gets exp(0) = 1. After rescaling by exp(20-40) = exp(-20), the best token from the old page contributes exp(-20) ≈ 2e-9 to the sum. The key insight: both algorithms should produce the same result because: - Batch: token with score 20 contributes exp(20 - 50) = exp(-30) ≈ 9e-14 - Online: token with score 20 (relative to max=20) contributes exp(0) = 1. Then rescaled by exp(20-40) = exp(-20) to give ~2e-9. Then rescaled again by exp(40-50) = exp(-10) = 4.5e-5, giving ~9e-14. Same! But the intermediate values (1 → 2e-9 → 9e-14) involve subnormal numbers or underflow in fp32. fp32 has a minimum normal value of ~1.2e-38, so 2e-9 is fine, and 9e-14 is also fine (it's subnormal but representable). So the numerical issue is NOT underflow — it's precision loss in the intermediate rescaling. When we compute `running_sum = running_sum * rescale + new_sum`, the `running_sum * rescale` term may be very small compared to `new_sum`, causing the addition to lose precision. For example: - running_sum (after rescaling once) = 2e-9 - new_sum from second page ≈ 1 (for the max-scoring token) + smaller contributions - running_sum * rescale2 = 2e-9 * 4.5e-5 = 9e-14 - running_sum + new_sum ≈ 1 + 9e-14 ≈ 1 (the 9e-14 is lost in fp32 addition!) This is the problem. When the max jumps significantly, the old contributions become negligible relative to the new ones, and their contribution is lost in floating-point addition. The batch softmax doesn't have this issue because all values are computed at once relative to the final max. For the large_q_kv case (8x scaling), score differences are 8x larger, making the max jumps 8x larger, which makes the rescale factors 8x smaller in log space (exp(-8x) vs exp(-x)). This amplifies the precision loss. This is a fundamental limitation of online softmax with large variations in scores across pages. The fix would be to use the "safe" online softmax variant, or to accumulate scores in double precision. Actually, let me reconsider. Is there an alternative? Instead of online softmax, I could: 1. Store all scores in global memory (1024 * sizeof(float) = 4KB per head) and do batch softmax 2. Use double precision for the running state 3. Use a "log-space" accumulator that doesn't underflow Option 1 is the most robust but wastes memory bandwidth (for the score writes). For a memory-bound kernel, this is undesirable. Option 2 (double precision for running_max, running_sum, acc) would help but might still have the same issue. Option 3: use a more numerically stable online softmax. The standard fix is to track the log-sum-exp instead of the sum, but that changes the accumulation formula. Actually, wait. Let me check if the reference's error is actually 0.094 or 0.022. Earlier, the check.py reported max_abs_diff = 0.094, but my test showed kernel vs ref for head 27 = 0.022. The difference might be that check.py tests different seeds or stress cases. Let me re-run the check for just the large_q_kv case and see the actual max across all shapes. Actually, I think the real fix is to accept that the online softmax introduces some numerical error with large inputs and to use a higher precision for the running state.
